12.10.2.  Introduction 
Pregnancy increases the risk of HIV progression, while HIV increases the risk for maternal complications from pregnancy and poses the risk of perinatal HIV transmission to the unborn fetus.  Mother to child transmission (MTCT) of HIV can occur during pregnancy, labor, delivery or postpartum through breastfeeding.  In the absence of any interventions, vertical HIV transmission rates approximate 35%, but fall below 5% with effective interventions [ WHO , 2010].  In the United States and other developed countries, 
the risk of perinatal infection has decreased from 25% without intervention to less than 2% with intervention [ WHO, 2012].  The HIV -infected mother who breastfeeds her 
infant while taking ARVs herself or giving ARVs to her infant reduces the risk of transmission to about 2% after 6 months of breastfeeding, or 4% over 12 months [UNAIDS , 2011]. 
The 2013 WHO  Guidelines thus recommend (strong recommendation, moderate-quality 
evidence) all pregnant and breastfeeding women with HIV should initiate triple ARVs (ART), which should be maintained at least for the duration of mother- to-child 
transmission risk. Women meeting treatment eligibility criteria should continue lifelong ART [ WHO , 2013]. The global benefits anticipated from ART in pregnant women who 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 250 
 are eligible for treatment include treatment of the mother’s underlying HIV disease, 
eliminating pediatric transmission/infection and reducing sexual transmission of HIV.  
Recent recommendation updates to treatment guidelines have included objectives to increase HIV screening of patients, including pregnant women (noting the importance of adopting HIV screening to be a part of prenatal care).  
The ART recommendation for pregnant females prioritizes the health of women over potential risks and increased cost.  For females who are on ARV therapy at the time that they become pregnant, the World Health Organization recommends that they continue such therapy if they are responding to the ARV. 
In line with this recommendation, this study will allow those females participating in 201584 who are receiving CAB + RPV LA  but become pregnant on study, to continue in 
the study in order to maintain their effective regimen with minimal disruption.  The PK of CAB + RPV LA , characterization of the safety of CAB + RPV LA  administered during 
pregnancy, and characterization of maternal, birth and infant outcomes following treatment with CAB + RPV LA will be examined .  
12.10.3.  Benefit/Risk Assessment  
Discuss with pregnant participant the benefit-risk of continuing in the study and continuing to receive CAB + RPV LA injections , or being withdrawn from study, as a 
result of her pregnancy. All participants who chose to stay in the study during pregnancy, and who choose to continue to receive CAB + RPV LA injections  will need to sign a 
pregnancy specific ICF addendum. 
There is a pregnancy exposure registry that monitors pregnancy outcomes in women 
exposed to CAB + RPV LA  (CABENUVA ) during pregnancy. Healthcare providers are 
encouraged to register all pregnant study participants, whether or not they choose to remain in the study, by calling the Antiretroviral Pregnancy Registry [ Antiretroviral 
Pregnancy Registry (APR) Steering Committee , 2013] at 1-800-258-4263. 
12.10.3.1.  Cabotegravir  
Cabotegravir use in pregnant women has not been evaluated and there are insufficient human data on the use of during pregnancy to adequately assess a drug- associated risk of 
birth defects and miscarriage.  
The rate of miscarriage is not reported in the APR. The background risk for major birth defects and miscarriage for the indicated population is unknown. The background rate for major birth defects in a U.S. reference population of the Metropolitan Atlanta Congenital Defects Program (MACDP) is 2.7%. The estimated background rate of miscarriage in clinically recognized pregnancies in the U.S. general population is 15% to 20%. The APR uses the MACDP as the U.S. reference population for birth defects in the general population. The MACDP evaluates women and infants from a limited geographic area and does not include outcomes for births that occurred at less than 20 weeks’ gestation. 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 251 
 Animal Data (pre- clinical)  
Cabotegravir was administered orally to pregnant rats at 0, 0.5, 5, or 1,000 mg/kg/day 
from 15 days before cohabitation, during cohabitation, and from Gestation Days 0 to 17. There were no effects on fetal viability when fetuses were delivered by caesarean  
although a minor decrease in fetal body weight was observed at 1,000 mg/kg/day (greater than 30 times the exposure in humans at the RHD). No drug- related fetal toxicities were 
observed at 5 mg/kg/day (approximately 13 times the exposure in humans at the R HD) 
and no drug- related fetal malformations were observed at any dose.  
Cabotegravir was administered orally to pregnant rabbits at 0, 30, 500, or 2,000 mg/kg/day from Gestation Days 7 to 19. No drug- related fetal toxicities were observed at 
2,000 mg/kg/day (approximately 0.7 times the exposure in humans at the RHD). 
In a rat pre- and postnatal development study, cabotegravir was administered orally to 
pregnant rats at 0, 0.5, 5, or 1,000 mg/kg/day from Gestation Day 6 to Lactation Day 21. A delay in the onset of parturition and increases in the number of stillbirths and neonatal deaths by Lactation Day 4 were observed at 1,000 mg/kg/day (greater than 30 times the exposure in humans at the RHD); there were no alterations to growth and development of surviving offspring. In a cross-fostering study, similar incidences of stillbirths and early postnatal deaths were observed when rat pups born to cabotegravir- treated mothers were 
nursed from birth by control mothers. There was no effect on neonatal survival of control pups nursed from birth by cabotegravir- treated mothers. A  lower dose of 5 mg/kg/day (13 
times the exposure at the RHD) was not associated with delayed parturition or neonatal mortality in rats. Studies in pregnant rats showed that cabotegravir crosses the placenta and can be detected in fetal tissue.  
During the pre-clinical development of CAB, there were no positive genotox findings. Embryo-fetal studies also showed no adverse findings including neural tube defects.  In a pre and postnatal study, there were some test article- related decreases in F1 pup  survival 
(87.4% vs 98.9% in control) in the highest dose (1000mg/kg/day) during postnatal days 1-4.  No findings in the 0, 0.5 and 5 mg/kg/day doses).  
The clinical significance of these finding in humans is unknown. 
Human Data  
Cabotegravir use in pregnant females has not been evaluated and there are insufficient 
human data on the use of CAB + RPV LA  during pregnancy to adequately assess a drug-
associated risk of birth defects and miscarriage.  
While there are insufficient human data to assess the risk of neural tube defects (NTDs) with exposure to CAB + RPV LA  during pregnancy, preliminary findings from an 
unscheduled analysis of a birth outcomes surveillance study conducted in Botswana (Tsepamo Study) and presented in May 2018 showed a higher than expected number of neural tube defects (NTDs) among newborns whose mothers were exposed to DTG based ART at conception.  DTG is a different molecule in the same integrase class of medications as CAB. A s of May 2018 four cases of neural tube defects were identified in 
426 infants born to mothers who were exposed to DTG-containing regimens from the 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 252 
 time of conception. In the same study, no infant born to a woman who started DTG 
during pregnancy had a neural tube defect, out of 2,824 women. Updated analysis of interim data from the Tsepamo study became available in 2019 and more recently in 2020. Subsequently, the study team presented an updated analysis, including data through to 30 April 2020, at the 23
rd International AIDS Society (IAS) Meeting [ Zash , 2020].  
The latest data from the Tsepamo study included additional data accrued between 1 April 2019 (the cut-off for the last formal analysis) and 30 April 2020. Over this 13-month period, 39,200 additional births were recorded, including 1908 additional exposures to DTG at conception. Two additional NTDs were detected in 1908 (0.10%) deliveries to mothers taking DTG at conception, compared with six NTDs in 4569 (0.13%) deliveries in mothers taking non-DTG regimens at conception, of which five NTDs in 2999 (0.17%) deliveries were to mothers taking efavirenz at conception. The incidence in HIV negative mothers over the 13-month period was 17/30,258 (0.06%).  
As of the Tsepamo April 2020 analysis, seven cases of neural tube defects were reported 
in 3,591 deliveries (0.19%) to mothers taking dolutegravir -containing regimens at the time of conception, compared with 21 cases in 19,361 deliveries (0.11%) to mother s 
taking non- dolutegravir containing regimens at the time of conception (Prevalence Difference 0.09%; 95% CI -0.03, 0.30).  Since the first analysis the estimated prevalence of neural tube defects with DTG exposure at conception has decreased in magnitude from 0.94% to 0.19%. In the same study, no increased risk of neural tube defects was reported in women who started dolutegravir during pregnancy. Two out of 4,448 deliveries (0.04%) to mothers who started dolutegravir during pregnancy had a neural tube de fect, 
compared with five out of 6,748 deliveries (0.07%) to mothers who started non-dolutegravir -containing regimens during pregnancy. 
A causal relationship of these events to the use of DTG has not been established.  The incidence of neural tube defects in the general population ranges from 0.5- 1 case per 
1,000 live births. There are insufficient human data on the use of CAB + RPV LA during 
pregnancy to adequately assess a drug- associated risk of miscarriage or birth defects, 
including NTDs. 
12.10.3.2.  Rilpivirine  
Animal Data  
Rilpivirine was administered orally to pregnant rats (40, 120, or 400 mg/kg/day) and rabbits (5, 10, or 20 mg/kg/day) through organogenesis (on Gestation Days 6 through 17, and 6 through 19, respectively).  No significant toxicological effects were observed in  
embryo- fetal toxicity studies performed with rilpivirine in rats and rabbits at exposures 
15 (rats) and 70 (rabbits) times the exposure in humans at the RHD . In a pre - and 
postnatal development study, rilpivirine  was administered orally up to 400 mg/kg/day 
through lactation. No  adverse effects were noted in the offspring  at maternal exposures 
up to 63 times the exposure in humans at the RHD 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 253 
 Human Data  
Based on prospective reports to the APR of over 390 exposures to oral rilpivirine-
containing regimens during the first trimester of pregnancy and over 170 during second/third trimester of pregnancy, the prevalence of birth defects in live births was 
1.3% (95% CI: 0.4% to 3.0%) and 1.1% (95% CI: 0.1% to 4.0%) following first and second/third trimester exposures. 
Available data from the APR show no difference in the overall risk of birth defects for 
rilpivirine compared with the background rate for major birth defects of 2.7% in a U.S. reference population of the Metropolitan Atlanta Congenital Defects Program (MAC DP) 
In a clinical trial, total oral rilpivirine exposures were generally lower during pregnancy compared with the postpartum period. Refer to Edurant  for additional information on 
rilpivirine . 
12.10.4.  Clinical Considerations  
12.10.4.1.  Exposure 
Lower exposures with oral rilpivirine were observed during pregnancy. Cabotegravir and rilpivirine  are detected in systemic circulation for up to 12 months or longer after 
discontinuing injections of CAB + RPV LA ; therefore, consideration should be given to 
the potential for fetal exposure during pregnancy.  
With the change in volume of distribution associated with pregnancy, drug concentrations of CAB and RPV during pregnancy will be assessed in pregnant participants who contiune to receive LA therapy while on study. For these participants, PK samples will be collected at every study visit throughout the duration of the pregnancy and at the first postpartum LA injection visit. Additionally, all other scheduled assessments will continue as reflected in as described in the protocol in the Time and Events Table ( see Section 
7.1.).

 12.10.4.2.  Use of Supplements with CAB + RPV LA  
During pregnancy, additional supplements including vitamins, minerals and other 
mediations including OTC meds may be prescribed to the pregnant woman. It is important for all female participants  who remain in the study to be aware of any potential 
DDIs that may occur with study medications and other agents used during pregnancy. 
Oral Cabotegravir Only  
Antacid products containing divalent cations (e.g., aluminium, calcium and magnesium) must be taken at least 2 hours before or at least 4 hours after CAB. 
Concurrent administration of multivitamins is acceptable.  
12.10.4.3.  Overall Benefit:Risk Conclusion  
All medications have AE profiles that must be assessed prior to use, allowing for an 
appropriate risk/benefit assessment.  Additional considerations when using CAB + RPV LA can be found in the protocol in Section 4.6. 
There is limited data regarding the use of CAB + RPV LA in pregnant females. Based on 
animal data, the use of CAB + RPV LA is not anticipated to increase the risk of adverse developmental or reproductive outcomes in humans.  Available data from the APR show no difference in the overall risk of birth defects for rilpivirine compared with the background rate for major birth defects of 2.7% in a U.S. reference population of the Metropolitan Atlanta Congenital Defects Program (MAC DP). 
Refer to Section 12.10.4.1. for additional data. 
The use of CAB + RPV LA during pregnancy may offer unique benefits. It is well 
documented that treatment adherence challenges to oral therapy exists both in the peri-partum and post-partum periods with LA dosing offering an opportunity to overcome such adherence challenges. LA therapy may also help with nausea (50 % mild to moderate) or hyperemesis (2%). Female participants  on LA dosing who become pregnant 
will have exposures throughout pregnancy due to the long half- life and PK tail of 
CAB/RPV. Pregnant participants who are withdrawn from study and are initiated on an alternative oral ART regimen consisting of either 2 or 3 antiretrovirals to protect the life of the mother and for the prevention of MTCT, potentially expose the fetus to additional ARVs durin g gestation (in some cases upwards of 5 antiretrovirals). 
In summary, taking into account the measures taken to minimize risk to participants participating in this study, the potential risks identified in association with CAB + RPV LA are justified by the anticipated benefits that may be afforded to pregnant participants  
with HIV infection.  
Given the risk/benefit ratio for CAB + RPV LA dosing in WCBP, coupled with concerns of increasing fetal exposure to several additional antiretrovirals upon participant withdrawal, pregnant participants will be allowed to remain in the study and continue to receive CAB + RPV LA injections, once the new pregnancy ICF addendum is signed by 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
256 
 the participant.  
 
12.10.5.  Study Assessments and Procedures: specific assessments for 
pregnant participants  
Participants who become pregnant while in the study, and who sign the informed consent pregnancy addendum may remain in the study and continue to receive CAB + RPV LA.  
Please note: The HIV provider is responsible for HIV care and will collaborate and share 
information with the subject’s obstetric care provider, discuss the subject’s participation in this study, the necessary procedures at delivery, to share HIV information, and to collect birth and infant outcomes from the subject’s obstetric care provider and/or the 
pediatric health provider for the infant. 
Because obstetric and/or pediatric care will not be specifically provided via this study, the 
subject must also establish appropriate obstetric and pediatric care (including prenatal care) per local standard of care (SoC) in parallel.  It will be necessary  for the subject to 
provide a release of medical information to facilitate collection of pregnancy and pregnancy outcomes by the investigator 
All assessments will be conducted in accordance with the protocol, Section 7, and as 
described in the Time and Events Table (see Section 7.1.).  
12.10.5.1.  Safety Assessments  
Pregnancy related complications and diagnoses, and outcomes will be captured as AEs and SAEs as outlined in the protocol in Section 7.4.3. 
Pregnancy complications (e.g., preeclampsia or eclampsia, prolonged hospitalization after 
delivery, for wound infections etc, seizures) and elective terminations for medical reasons must be reported as an AE or SAE.  Spontaneous abortions must be reported as an SAE.  
In the event of a pregnancy loss, after the loss is confirmed the subject may continue to receive CAB + RPV LA unless they meet the criteria for confirmed virologic withdrawal.  They may continue to CAB + RPV LA until study medications are locally approved and commercially available or until they no longer receive benefit.  In this case the subject 
must agree to use contraception to avoid a ‘new’ pregnancy (See Appendix 7 of the protocol). 
Any SAE occurring in association with the pregnancy brought to the investigator’s 
attention after the subject has completed the study and considered by the investigator as possibly related to the study treatment, must be promptly reported to GSK 
12.10.5.2.  Pharmacokinetics  
Refer to Section 7.5. in the protocol. 
All pregnant participants who elect to remain in the study will have the following PK 
samples obtained at each LA injection visit throughout the pregnancy and at the first 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
257 
 postpartum LA injection visit:  
• Blood samples for evaluation of total CAB (2mL each) and total RPV (2mL each) 
plasma PK concentrations.  
• Blood sample for evaluation of unbound CAB (9mL each) plasma PK concentration. 
All PK samples will be trough levels and will be collected prior to the scheduled LA injection. The pre-dose trough PK sample is to be collected within 15 minutes prior to the LA dose, on the day of the study visit.  
For participants pregnant during the Long Term Follow Up Phase, plasma concentrations 
of cabotegravir and rilpivirine will be collected as per 7.1 Time and Events table.  
Please refer to the SPM for PK sample collection, processing, and shipping instructions. The actual date and time of each PK sample collection will be recorded in the eCRF.

 12.11.  Appendix 11: Device Deficiencies: Definition and 
Procedures for Recording, Evaluating, Follow-up, and 
Reporting in Medical Device Studies 
The definitions and procedures detailed in this appendix are in accordance with ISO 
14155, European Medical Device Regulation (MDR) 2017/745 for clinical device research, and the US Food and Drug Administration (FDA) combination product reporting rule, 21 CFR 4, Subpart B. 
Both the investigator and the sponsor will comply with all local medical device reporting 
requirements for medical devices.  
The detection and documentation procedures described in this protocol apply to all medical devices used in the study (see Section 6.14 for the list of medical devices).  
12.11.1.  Definition of Device Deficiency  
Device Deficiency Definition  
• A device deficiency is an inadequacy of a medical device with respect to its identity, quality, durability, reliability, safety, or performance. Device deficiencies include malfunctions, use errors, and information supplied by the manufacturer. 
12.11.2.  Recording and Follow -Up of Device Deficiencies  
Device Deficiency Recording  
• When a device deficiency occurs, with or without an associated AE/SAE, it is the investigator’s responsibility to review all applicable documentation (e.g., hospital progress notes, laboratory reports, and diagnostics reports) related to the event. 
• The investigator will then record all relevant device deficiency information on the appropriate form. If applicable, any associated AE or SAE will be documented in the participant’s medical records, in accordance with the investigator’s standard clinical p ractice.  
• There may be instances when copies of medical records for certain cases are requested by the sponsor. In this case, all participant identifiers, with the exception of the participant number, will be redacted on the copies of the medical records before submission to the sponsor. 
• The investigator will attempt to fully describe the device deficiency and provide details on any treatment provided.  
• For device deficiencies, it is very important that the investigator describe any corrective or remedial actions taken to prevent the deficiency’s recurrence.  
o A remedial action is any action other than routine maintenance or servicing of a medical device where such action is necessary to prevent the recurrence of a device deficiency. This includes any amendment to the device design to prevent recurrence.  
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 259 
 Assessment of Intensity of associated AE/SAEs  
• If an AE or SAE is associated with a device deficiency, the investigator will make 
an assessment of intensity for each AE or SAE as outlined in Section 12.6.5. 
Follow -up of device deficiency  
• The investigator is obligated to perform or arrange for the conduct of supplemental 
measurements and/or evaluations as medically indicated or as requested by the 
sponsor to elucidate the nature of the device deficiency and any associated AE or SAE as fully as possible 
• New or updated information regarding the device deficiency will be recorded in the originally completed medical device deficiency report form.  
• If there is an associated SAE with the device deficiency, the investigator will submit any updated SAE data to GSK within 24 hours of receipt of the information.

 Sub- study Protocol Amendment Title: An Amendment to the FLAIR Study to Evaluate 
the Pharmacokinetics, Safety, Tolerability, Maintenance of Virological Suppression and 
Patient Reported Outcomes for Participants Receiving Cabotegravir (CAB 200 mg/mL) and Rilpivirine (300 mg/mL) Long- Acting Inj ections Following Sub- cutaneous (SC) 
Administration in the Anterior Abdominal Wall SC Tissue  Compared with Intramuscular 
(IM) Administration in the Gluteus Medius Muscle in Adult Participants Living with HIV -
1 infection in the FLAIR Study.  
12.12.1.  Sub- Study Amendment Background 
Cabotegravir/rilpivirine (CAB/RPV) long acting (LA) intramuscular (IM) injection has 
been approved as a two- drug regimen for the treatment of HIV -1 infection in treatment 
experienced adults and adolescents, virologically suppressed on an orally administere d 
regimen, who switch to long- acting therapy. CAB/RPV LA is currently administered in the 
clinic as monthly or every two months dosing for intramuscular gluteal injections  by a health care provider.    As more HIV -infected individuals opt for LA therapy to control their HIV infection, there 
has been interest in research and development of potential options to allow for at -home-
based therapy administered by the patient via an auto- injector or pre -filled s yringe. In 
assessing options for home based self -administration, data needs to be generated evaluating 
pharmacokinetics, safety and tolerability, virologic response and patient report outcomes of cabotegravir and rilpivirine LA following sub- cutaneous (SC)  administration. Assessing 
the utility of SC injections in an existing study like FLAIR is an efficient pathway to evaluate and compare these parameters among study participants with ongoing experience receiving CAB and RPV LA via IM administration. To all ow for self- administration, the 
sub-cutaneous tissue of the anterior abdomen   is an easily accessible location  and will be the subcutaneous site  utilized in the FLAIR SC amendment (sub-study).    While the ultimate aim of self -administration would be via an auto- injector or pre -filled 
syringe (under development), the FLAIR SC amendment (sub- study) will require HCP 
administered injections via a SC approach in the subcutaneous tissue of the anterior abdomen)  compared with HCP administered IM gluteal injections in the gluteus medius.  The currently approved IM formulations for CAB (200 mg/mL) and RPV (300 mg/mL), as also used in the FLAIR parent study, will be utilized to assess both IM and SC routes of administration.   
12.12.1.1.  Data Utilizing CAB 200/mL Subcutaneously (SC)  
Two phase I studies have reported the tolerability, safety, and pharmacokinetics of cabotegravir long- acting injection administered intramuscularly or via a sub-cutaneous 
route [Spreen et al; J Acquir Immune Defic Syndr 2014;67:481–486)]. In a randomized, placebo -controlled, double -blinded, single -dose study, 58 HIV -uninfected adults received 
cabotegravir as a gluteal intramuscular injection of 100 mg, 200 mg, 400 mg or 800 mg (administered as two equally divided split injections) or as a subcutaneous abdom inal 
injection of 100 mg, 200 mg or 400 mg (administered as two equally divided split 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 262 
 injections) or as a placebo injection vehicle. Following single intramuscular or 
subcutaneous injection, plasma drug concentrations increased rapidly over the first week, with sustained mean plasma concentrations above the PA –IC
90 for approximately 24 weeks 
or longer for doses of at least 200 mg, as shown in Figure 11  
Figure 11  Mean plasma levels of GSK1265744 over time following single -dose 
administration of long -acting formulation.  
 
Figure 11 . GSK1265744 (200 mg/ml) was administered as a single IM (gluteal) or SC (abdominal) 
injection or equally divided IM or SC injection. Each cohort comprised eight healthy adult patients (six 
active/two placebo). The dashed line represents the plasma PA -IC90 value for GSK1265744 against wild-
type HIV -1 of 0.166 mg/ml.  
CAB was detected in plasma for up to 48 weeks. Following LA injections, mean 
absorption- limited apparent terminal- phase half -life ranged from 21 to 50 days as 
compared to approximately 40 h following single -dose oral administration. This longer 
apparent ha lf-life following injection is a result of low solubility of the drug particle, 
prompting a slow absorption rate of drug from the injectable formulation with no change in the plasma elimination half -life of the dissolved active drug.  
When the injectable formulation was administered as two equally divided, split dose injections (Cohort 4, 400 mg x 2 intramuscular and Cohort 7, 200 mg x 2 subcutaneous), total drug release was increased so that the maximum observed plasma concentration (Cmax) was greater than dose proportional and there was a more pronounced decay in drug 
concentrations over time. However, overall extent of exposure [area under the curve (AUC) from time zero to infinity] was dose proportional and did not change ( Table 18).  
Additionally, using a power model, PK parameters seemed to increase proportionally to dose after unsplit SC administration (100 and 200 mg).  Administration of the dose as 2 

TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 263 
 separate injections (dose splitting) — 400 mg (200 mg x 2) IM and SC as well as 800 mg 
(400 mg x 2) IM—achieved geometric mean Cw4 above the protein-adjusted IC 90.  
Table 18  Plasma CAB PK Parameter Summary  
 
Although no formal statistical analysis of cabotegravir PK parameters by gender was 
performed, there was a general trend of higher plasma exposures in female subjects after SC administration of cabotegravir and of higher exposures in males after split IM injections. Gender differences in absorption rate after IM injections may reflect greater 
skin- to-muscle depth in females, which would result in an increased likelihood of 
delivering cabotegravir into the SC space. 
Safety and Tolerability  
Thirty -eight (79%) of 48 subjects receiving an IM injection and 22 (92%) of 24 subjects 
receiving a SC injection reported at least 1 AE. A higher percentage of AEs identified as ISRs occurred in subjects receiving CAB than placebo. In subjects receiving IM  injections, 
33 (83%) of 40 subjects receiving CAB reported an AE compared with 5 (63%) of 8 subjects receiving placebo, whereas in subjects receiving SC injections, 17 (94%) of 18 subjects receiving CAB reported an AE compared with 5 (83%) of 6 subjects r eceiving 
placebo. Most frequent (>2 subjects in any dose cohort) AEs that occurred while on therapy by treatment are shown in Table 19. 
The most common adverse events were self -limited injection site reactions (ISR). ISRs 
were generally mild, with pain and erythema at the injection site reported as the most 
common findings for both IM and SC administration. Erythema, however, was more comm only reported after SC administration compared with IM. While nodule formation 
was also seen after both IM and SC administrations, it too was more commonly reported after SC vs IM dosing. While ISR of pain did not increase in incidence with increasing volume after IM administration (from 0.5 to 2.0 mL), pain was more commonly reported with increasing volume after SC administration (0.5 to 1.0 mL). There were no systemic serious or grade 3 to 4 adverse events (see Table 19 ). 
Specific to SC -related ISRs, pain was described in 50%, 100%, and 83% of subjects 

TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 264 
 receiving CAB SC 100 mg, 200 mg, or 400 mg split injections, respectively, relative to 
33% of placebo subjects describing pain. The mean duration of pain ranged from 7 to 12 days. Erythema was described in 33%, 83%, and 67% of subjects receiving CAB SC 100 mg, 200 mg, or 400 mg split injections, respectively, relative to 17% of subjects receiving SC placebo injection. The mean duration of erythema ranged from 2 to 10.7 days.  
Overall, cabotegravir was generally safe and well tolerated when administered as a single or separate IM injection from 100 to 800 mg and as a single SC injection from 100 to 400 mg. ISRs were reported by most subjects; however, they were all mild (grade 1) in severity. In addition, ISRs were self- limited, no subjects required symptomatic treatment, and there 
were no withdrawals due to ISRs. The incidence of ISRs seemed to be related to active drug as a higher percentage of AEs occurred in subjects who received cabotegravir than placebo. There were no substantial differences in reporting of non- ISR AEs between 
cabotegravir and placebo [Spreen et al, 2014].

In a second phase I study, HIV -negative adults received a 14 -day lead -in of oral 
cabotegravir 30 mg per day to assess safety and tolerability before administration of the long-acting injection [Spreen et al, 2014].  
Patients were randomized into one of four cohorts: all received cabotegravir 800 mg 
intramuscular (as 400 mg x 2) as a loading dose followed by three monthly doses of 200 mg subcutaneous (Cohort 1); 200 mg intramuscular (Cohort 2); 400 mg intramuscular (Co hort 
3); or after 3 months, a single further injection of 800 mg intramuscular (Cohort 4). Cohorts 2 and 3 also received gluteal intramuscular doses of rilpivirine LA at months 3 (1200 mg) and 4 (900 or 600 mg, respectively). Forty -seven patients enrolled,  with 40 patients 
receiving at least one long -acting injection; 38 completed all planned injections. Seven 
patients discontinued the oral lead- in phase, six for non-drug- related reasons and one for 
an adverse event (dizziness following first 30 mg dose).

12.12.1.2.  Data Utilizing RPV LA Subcutaneously (SC)  
A phase 1 study of rilpivirine LA with a previous 100 mg/ml nanosuspension evaluated the 
pharmacokinetics and safety of single gluteal intramuscular or abdominal subcutaneous injections in 51 HIV -negative adult participants at doses of 200, 400 and 600 mg, vehicle 
(placebo) or saline [ Verloes  R, 2008]. An additional nine patients received a single 400 mg 
IM injection or saline into the deltoid muscle. Consistent with the preclinical experience, rilpivirine was slowly released from the injection site into plasma, with drug concentrations of more than 10 ng/ml for 12–26 weeks. Dose proportionality and similar plasma concentration –time profiles were observed for both subcutaneous and gluteal 
intramuscular injections (see Figure 13 and Table 23). ISRs consisted of redness, bruising, 
pain and to a lesser extent, induration, and were more frequent with active drug injections versus placebo. There was a greater frequency of ISRs with subcutaneous as compared to intramuscular administration. Among i ntramuscular injections, gluteal injections were 
better tolerated than deltoid injections. There were no serious adverse events or grade 3 or 4 adverse events.

Preliminary short-term data of an ongoing Phase 1 study in healthy adult participants with 
the current commercial RPV LA 300  mg/mL formulation 
(https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/[STUDY_ID_REMOVED]) suggest that RPV plasma concentrations in the first month after  SC administration of RPV LA may be somewhat 
lower compared to historical data for IM administration. Modelling and simulation was used to estimate what the impact could be for HIV -infected patients on monthly CAB+RPV 
at steady -state switching from IM to S C administration, as planned in this sub- study. A 
conservative estimate of 50% lower bioavailability for SC administration compared to IM administration was used. Even with an estimated 50% lower bioavailability, it is predicted that after 3 RPV LA 600 mg SC injections, administrated a month apart each time, the RPV 
plasma concentrations would still remain above those observed for the every 2 months IM dosing regimen, which has been shown to be efficacious. As a cautionary measure for this exploratory sub-s tudy, however, the visit window for the SC administrations will be 
reduced to only allow injections to be administered up to one week earlier (as opposed to allowing injections one week earlier through one week later) and will not allow injections to be ad ministered up to one week later.

12.12.2.  Sub- Study Amendment Rationale  
Data from several Phase 1, healthy volunteer studies assessing various doses of CAB 
200 mg/mL and RPV 100 mg/mL administered subcutaneously demonstrated similar plasma PK parameters to intramuscular dosing with achieved concentrations above the PA -
IC
90 for both drugs. For CAB, the geomean Ctau after 200 mg administered SC was 
1.61 µ g/mL and was 1.66 µ g/mL after 200 mg administered IM suggesting that switching 
400 mg IM with SC dosing will likely result in similar CAB plasma concentrations and above those shown to be efficacious for the every 2 months IM dosing regimen.  For the 300 mg/mL formulation of RPV, prior data suggest that concentrations after SC administration could either be similar or somewhat lower compared to IM administration. Modelling and simulation showed that even when using a conservative estimation of 50% lower bioavailability for SC administration compared to IM administration, it is predicted that after 3 monthly RPV LA 600 mg SC injections, the RPV plasma concentrations would still rema in above those observed for the every 2 months IM dosing regimen, which has 
been shown to be efficacious. 
Co-administration of both CAB and RPV was generally safe and well tolerated, with the 
most reported AEs classified as grade 1. SC administration was overall less well tolerated 
than IM injections with higher frequency of ISRs being reported after SC administration compared with IM administration although there were no SAEs or grade 3 or  4 AEs 
reported with SC administration. These data provided an initial assessment of SC 

TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 270 
 administration of LA CAB and RPV in healthy volunteers and allows for further evaluation 
of SC dosing of LA CAB and RPV in HIV-infected individuals.   The FLAIR study is a large, on- going, Phase 3 clinical study that assessed monthly LA IM 
dosing of CAB and RPV compared with an orally administered standard of care regimen in treatment naïve subjects, all of whom received 20 weeks of oral induction therapy with abacavir/dolutegravir/lamivudine prior to being randomized to either continue with abacavir/dolutegravir/lamivudine therapy or to switch to long- acting CAB/RPV. For those 
randomized at baseline to LA therapy, a 4 -week oral lead in with CAB (30  mg) a nd RPV 
(25 mg) was required to assess tolerability prior to proceeding with LA therapy [ Orkin , 
NEJM,  2020]. Since participants in the FLAIR study were randomized either at baseline to 
LA therapy or were given the opportunity to transition to LA therapy in the extension phase of FLAIR at week 100 (either with or without an OLI), participants enrolling into the FLAIR sub -study would have been exposed to LA therapy for a minimum of at least 12 
months (for those starting LA in the extension phase of FLAIR, with LSLV for the Week 124 endpoint having occurred on 21 -FEB-2020) to over three years (those originally 
randomized at the start of FLAIR to the LA arm).   In addition to PK and safety parameters, other important outcome measures to be assessed in the FLAIR sub -study include the ability to maintain virologic suppression for 
participants who transition from IM to SC injections as well as several important patient -
reported outcomes including a preference questionnaire that aims to assess participants’ preference for SC vs IM injections and reasons for such a preference.   The use of SC injections in the on- going FLAIR study allows an efficient pathway for 
evaluation of the two routes of administration of CAB and RPV LA as alternative approaches to injectable HIV treatment. This approach will generate important data to infor m future development of a patient self -administered option of CAB and RPV LA. 
Therefore, the FLAIR study has been amended to allow an assessment of IM versus SC injections for participants who are currently in the extension phase of FLAIR and are receiving  maintenance dosing of CAB with the 200 mg/mL formulation (2  mL=400 mg) 
along with RPV 300 mg/mL formulation (2  mL=600  mg).    
 The window period around the administration of SC dosing will be up to 7 days earlier but will not allow injections to be given up to one week later.  This is different from what is allowed in the FLAIR parent study ( -7 to +7 days) and is due to data emerging from an on-
going healthy volunteer study of RPV 300 mg that suggests RPV plasma concentrations in the first month after SC administration of RPV LA may be somewhat lower compared to historical data for IM administration but still above those observed for the every 2 months IM dosing regimen, which has been shown to be efficacious. 
Overall outcomes being measured include PK parameters Ctau, concentrations 1 -week post 
dose (~Cmax), and area under the curve [AUC (0- tau)]); safety, tolerability, virologic 
response and various patient reported outcomes including Numerical Rating Scale (N RS); 
HIV Treatment Satisfaction Questionnaire c and s (HIVTSQc and HIVTSQs ); Perception 
of Injection (PIN), a preference questionnaire and various exploratory objectives including  reasons to switch from IM to SC in HIV -1 infected participants receiving CAB and RPV 
LA administered via SC versus IM injections.

 271 
 12.12.2.1.  Data on CAB/RPV Subcutaneous Injection Site Reactions  
The FLAIR SC sub -study will be the first study in HIV -infected individuals and will 
assess the safety, tolerability and various PK parameters after SC administration of 
CAB/RPV for subjects currently enrolled in FLAIR who opt to enroll (after screening in) into this sub-study. Several prior Phase 1, healthy volunteer studies have individually assessed SC administration of CAB and RPV and have demonstrated overall tolerability after SC dosing with the most commonly reported ISRs being pain, erythema and nodular formation. These ISRs tended to be self-limited, have been mostly grade 1 and grade 2.  
Specifically, two Phase 1 studies investigated CAB200 mg/mL administered 
subcutaneously, with single and multiple dose studies ranging from 200-400 mL [Spreen et al., 2014; Spreen et al., 2014]. A Phase 1 FTIH healthy volunteer study (212482) assessed vari ous doses and routes of administration of a 400mg formulation of 
cabotegravir with IM injections administered into the gluteal and thigh muscles and SC injections administrated into the anterior abdominal muscle, with up to 1.5 mL of volume administered su bcutaneously (600mg total dose of CAB 400mg/mL formulation). 
Specific to the SC arm of study 212482, no SAEs were reported with 1/9 participants reporting a grade 3 ISR of rednes/erythema leading to withdrawal. Maximum grade ISRs for all other SC participa nts were grade 1 (2/9) and grade 2 (6/9).   
Finally, an ongoing study supported by Janssen (TMC278LAHTX1003) is assessing 3mL of the standard RPV formulation (G001 at 300mg/mL) dosed SC. While the study is still ongoing, the initial assessment of the ISR data received to date have shown that almost all subjects experienced an ISR, although most were grade 1 or 2 with no grade 3 or higher ISRs being reported. The majority of these ISRs were classified as erythema, induration, pain, swelling or nodules. Given the results from these healthy volunteer studies, the sub-study team does not anticipate an ISR profile to be any different in a 
HIV-infected population than what was seen in the healthy volunteer studies detailed 
above. However, since the FLAIR SC sub-study will be the first study to assess SC dosing of CAB and RPV in HIV-infected individuals, the study team has developed ISR monitoring/pausing criteria (detailed in Section 12.12.4.7) that will be applied in the FLAIR sub -study.  
12.12.2.2.  ISR Monitoring Criteria Process  
Most ISRs observed in the healthy volunteer studies were either due to erythema, pain, induration or nodules.  Therefore, these typical and anticipated ISRs will not be considered as part of the criteria that leads to an ISR monitoring/pausing criteria. 
However, the ISR monitoring/pausing criteria will be applied when considering the 
incidence of ISRs of interest following SC dosing of CAB+RPV, detailed in Section 12.12.4.7.  
After 50% of participants (equating to 25 out of the expected 50) have experienced their 
first SC injection and after the Week 1 follow-up visit an in- stream safety data cut will be 
performed for ISR data including site reports of details of ISRs of interest. The posterior probability that the rate of ISRs of interest is > 0.05 will be calculated based on ISRs of interest collected through Week 1 for each participant. A target rate of 0.05 was chosen as it would be the equivalent of >1 participant out of 25 having an ISR of interest. If the Bayesian posterior probability that the true rate of ISRs of interest is >0.05 is low (< 5%), 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 272 
 then individual ISRs will undergo standard safety review. However, if the Bayesian 
posterior probability that the true rate of ISRs of interest is >0.05 is high (>5%), then a formal review of all ISR safety data will take place by the ViiV Safety and Label ing 
Committee (the VSLC) with the potential consideration to pause SC injections. If 1 or 2 participants experience an ISR of interest, these individual cases will be assessed and discussed with the FLAIR Medical Monitor and the Clinical Development Lead f or the 
CAB Treatment Program to determine whether to continue SC dosing for such participants. However, if 3 or more participants experience an ISR of interest, this would produce a study likelihood rate of 0.12, leading to posterior probability of >5%. Thus, as enrollment is staggered by country, if 3 participants experience an ISR of interest prior to 25 participants reaching the Week 1 visit, VSLC review will automatically be triggered, no matter when the ISR of interest occurs. Otherwise, VSLC will only be triggered based on the interim posterior probability. An evidence threshold of 5% gives us 95% confidence that the true rate of ISRs of interest is not >0.05 should our interim posterior probability not trigger a decision to bring forth formal VSLC review.   
Table 24 and Figure 15 below show predictions of our potential to make a decision to 
formally monitor with 95% confidence based on 1000 simulations with 50 participants. Likelihood data was simulated based on the binomial distribution with a potential response of failure vs non-failure given the various levels of true rate of ISRs of interest. A conjugate beta prior with parameters of a=0.001 (# of failures) and b=79 (# of successes) was selected based on participant level data from the previous studies mentioned and, as no previous ISRs of interest have been noted, a failure count of 0.001 is being used conservatively for modeling purposes. As seen in Table 24, if the true rate of ISRs of interest is 0.05, then we have a 23.3% chance of formal VSLC review while if the true rate is 0.08 or higher, we have a >50% chance of formal VSLC review.

 273

Interest  
 
Note: The vertical reference line indicates the target acceptable rate of ISRs of interest at 
0.05. The horizontal reference line indicates the posterior probability evidence threshold of formal VSLC review at 5%.

12.12.4.  Sub- Study FLAIR Amendment Design  
The FLAIR amendment (sub-study) will consist of three phases including a Screening/IM 
Gluteal injection Phase (T -4 weeks with 1 gluteal injection interval of 4 weeks), a Sub-
Cutaneous Abdominal Injection Phase (12 weeks with 3 injection intervals of 4 weeks each) and a Return to Intramuscular Gluteal Injection Phase (8 weeks with 2 injection intervals of 4 weeks each). 80 participants will be targeted for enrollment in order to reach the 30-50 necessary to assess the primary PK endpoint as well as to achieve a more robust safety conclusion. At the conclusion of the sub- study, participants will have the option to 
continue on the FLAIR parent study or if commercial access is available, the participant can transition off the sub- study, complete their participation in the FLAIR study and 
proceed directly to commercially sourced CAB/RPV LA treatment.

12.12.4.2.  Screening Phase (Gluteal IM)  
During the screening phase for the sub- study, participants will receive an  IM injection 
while being screened for the sub- study. Eligibility criteria must be assessed at the 
Screening Visit and confirmed prior to the first SC injection. Participants who ar e enrolled 
in the sub- study and subsequently withdraw from the parent FLAIR study for any reason 
may not be re -screened. Screening procedures should occur within 35 days prior to Day 1 
of the first dose in the SC Abdominal Injection Phase.  
After the Screening Visit/Gluteal Injection Visit, participants will need to return to the 
clinic 1 week later to obtain PK sampling as outlined in the Sub- Study Time and Events 
Table in Section 12.12.5. 
12.12.4.3.  Sub-Cutaneous Abdominal Injection Phase (12 Weeks)  
After confirming eligibility into the sub -study, participants will enter into the Sub-
Cutaneous Abdominal Injection Phase and receive a sub- cutaneous injection of CAB LA 
(2 mL; 400 mg) and RPV LA (2 mL; 600 mg) at the following visits:  
• Day 1  
• Week 4  
• Week 8  
The window period around the administration of SC dosing will be up to one week earlier  
and will not allow injections to be given up to one week later ( -7 days only without the 
allowance of a +7 day dosing window)  
Participants will need to return to the clinic 1 week after each  injection for PK sampling 
as outlined in the Sub-Study Time and Events Table in Section 12.12.5. 
12.12.4.4.  Return to Intramuscular Gluteal Injection Phase 
Following 12 weeks of SC injections, participants will return to the clinic to receive an IM 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 285 
 gluteal injection of CAB LA (2  mL; 400 mg) and RPV LA (2 mL; 600 mg) at the following 
visits:  
• Week 12 ( -7 days) 
• Week 16 (+/ -7 days) 
Participants will complete 8 weeks (2 injections cycles) of CAB/RPV LA therapy. After 
the Week 20 pre -dose assessments are obtained (AEs, SAEs and concomitant medications)  
the participant’s participation in the sub -study will have concluded.  
12.12.4.5.  Sub-Study Completion  
Participants are considered to have completed the sub- study once the final Week 20 pre -
dose assessments (AEs, SAEs and concomitant medications) are obtained. The IM injection and all other assessments will be considered part of the parent study and assessm ents should be completed as per the parent study time and events table in Section 
7.1. 
Depending on the local availability of the marketed product in each country, after the sub-
study is completed, and based on the particular country the participant is enrolled from, such participants in:  
• Countries where CAB LA+RPV LA marketed product is not yet locally 
available : Continue in the Extension Phase of the parent study and complete 
study visits as per the Time and Events table in Section 7.1. 
• Countries where CAB LA+RPV LA marketed product is locally available : 
Transition to CAB LA + RPV LA marketed product or an alternative ART as indicated below:  
o After the pre- injection assessments are completed at Week 20, the 
participant will receive the last IM gluteal injection as part of the parent  study. 
o Participant will complete the Safety Follow Up Visit 2 -4 weeks after the 
last injections (please refer to Section 5.5 of the protocol) before 
transitioning to a marketed ART.  
Note: If the participant has to withdraw from the study due to safety related reasons once CAB LA + RPV LA marketed product is locally available (see Section 5.4) the subjects would need to complete a withdrawal visit and enter the Long Term Follow Up Phase (see Section 4.2.6.).  
12.12.4.6.  Sub-Study Amendment Withdrawal/Stopping Criteria  
Participants meeting Withdrawal/Stopping criteria as per Section 5.4. will discontinue the study treatment and be withdrawn from both FLAIR and the sub-study, and will complete all assessments per the Time & Events table in Section 7.1. and enter in the Long Term Follow- Up Phase.  
Participants who decide to discontinue their participation in the sub- study for non- safety 
reasons (refer to Section 5.5.), including participants who require Oral Bridging  during 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 286 
 the sub-study or participants who decide to discontinue their participation in the sub -study 
due to injection -site (abdominal) related tolerability reasons:  
• In countries were the marketed products of CAB and RPV LA are not yet locally 
available, such patients will be allowed to transition back to the parent study and 
continue with IM gluteal injections per the randomized dosing schedule. 
• In countries were the marketed products of CAB and RPV LA are locally available : 
patients will be invited to return to gluteal injections in the parent  study and receive 1 more gluteal injections (additional injections might be required if requested by the Medical Monitor) before transitioning to marketed product as described in Section 5.5. 
12.12.4.7.  Sub-Study Injection Site Reactions  
For IM administrations, injection site reactions (ISRs) should be assessed as per the parent study instructions in Section 7.4.1. and Section 7.4.10.10. 
For SC administrations, any participant who experiences an ISR meeting the below 
criteria must be discussed with both the Medical Monitor and the Clinical Development Lead for CAB Treatment. These are ISRs of interest and will be included when considering the ISR monitoring/pausing criteria, as mentioned in Section 12.12.2.2.:  
• A Grade 4 injection site reaction.  
• An ISR of at least Grade 3 in severity where the ISR AE includes any of the following: 
o Ulceration  
o Secondary infection 
o Phlebitis  
o Sterile abscess  
o Drainage  
 
ISRs that are Grade 3 based upon the size of erythema or induration alone or based upon 
pain or symptoms causing inability to perform usual social & functional activities will be not be included for the purpose of the ISR monitoring/pausing criteria but wi ll be 
reviewed and considered when reviewing the ISR data. 
For SC administration, injection site erythema, redness, induration and swelling will be 
assessed by calculating both the length and width of the affected area.  
Any ISR associated with SC administration of CAB/RPV should be followed to 
resolution. 
Digital photographs may be documented, where possible, on all participants who have an 
injection site reaction, with observable findings, that is either serious or Grade 3 or higher, or that persist beyond 2 weeks.  Dermatology will be consulted on all par ticipants 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
 287 
 who have an injection site reaction considered serious, Grade 3 or above, or if clinically 
significant and persistent beyond 30 days and others if the Investigator or Medical Monitor feels it is medically necessary.  
 
12.12.4.8.  Sub-Study Amendment Specific Virological Failure Guidance  
Refer to Section 5.4.3., Section 5.4.4., and Section 5.4.5. 
12.12.4.9.  Sub-Study Amendment HIV -1 RNA Blips Guidance 
Guidance on SVF management can be found in Section 5.4.5.1.  
The Medical Monitor should discuss all cases of viral blips (defined as HIV -1 RNA 
≥50 c/mL and <200 c/mL)  with the site PI to assess whether any recent vaccinations were 
administered (within 4 weeks of blip) or any intercurrent illnesses developed (within 2-4 
weeks of the viral blip) that can spuriously elevate viral load. If there are possible alternative causes for the viral blip, further guidance will be provided by the Medical Monitor in these instances.  
Participants who have an HIV -1 RNA ≥50 c/mL and <200 c/mL during the SC Injection 
Phase of the sub- study, with no alternative cause for the viral blip identified, will need to 
have a repeat viral load assessment 2 -4 weeks after the initial viral blip for c onfirmation.  
If the repeat HIV -1 RNA is confirmed (≥50 c/mL and <200 c/mL) in participants with no 
recent history of vaccinations or intercurrent illnesses, the participant will have to withdraw 
from the SC sub- study and return to IM dosing in the parent study, or, if access is available, 
continue IM dosing via a commercial source.  
If the repeat VL is not confirmed (i.e, HIV -RNA is < 50  c/mL), the participant can continue 
the sub-study.  
If the repeat VL is ≥  200 c/mL, the participant has achieved a Suspected Virologic Failure 
and see Section 5.4.5.1 for further details  
Participants who have a viral blip (HIV -1 RNA ≥50  c/mL and <200 c/mL) during the IM 
Injection Phase of the sub- study including during the Return to Gluteal Injection Phase, 
see Section 5.4.5.1 of the parent study for further details on the management of HIV -1 
RNA blips.  
12.12.4.10.  Sub-Study Amendment Specific Withdrawal Criteria – Pregnancy  
If a subject becomes pregnant during the sub-study, the subject will need to withdraw 
from the sub-study and will have the option to continue with gluteal injections in the parent FLAIR study after signing a pregnancy-specific ICF addendum or be withdrawn from FLAIR. Please refer to Appendix 10 for additional information.

 12.12.6.  Sub- Study Health Outcomes Questionnaires  
12.12.6.1.  Sub-Study: Value Evidence and Outcomes  
Health outcomes assessments will be conducted according to the Time and Events Table 
(Section 12.12.5.). Assessments are recommended to be administered with a paper 
instrument at the beginning of the visit (except for NRS which is performed after the injections) prior to collection of blood for analysis and other scheduled assessments. There will be five health outcome measurements that will be administered during the sub-study including Numerical Rating Scale (NRS), HIVTSQc, HIVTSQs, PIN, and a Preference questionnaire. 
12.12.6.2.  Numerical Rating Scale (NRS)  
A numeric rating scale was used to assess the level of pain experienced following SC vs IM injections with CAB + RPV. The scale contains one item, and the response scale is ranging from 0= “no pain” to 10= “extreme pain”. The NRS was used to assess maximum level of pain on the day of the injection as well as maximum level of pain one week following injection. NRS questionnaires should be collected 30 to 60 minutes post injection.  
12.12.6.3.  HIV Treatment Satisfaction Questionnaire (HIVTSQ)  
HIVTSQ is a self -completion measure specifically designed to measure treatment 
satisfaction in PLHIV. It explores multiple aspects of treatment satisfaction including side effects, treatment demands, convenience, flexibility and understanding of HIV.  
There are two versions of this questionnaire: HIVTSQs and HIVTSQc.  HIVTSQs (status version)  is needed to measure absolute level of satisfaction while the 
HIVTSQ change version (HIVTSQc) was developed to overcome ceiling effects associated 
with HIVTSQs and enhance sensitivity to change by allowing those who were optimally (or close to optimally) satisfied at baseline to express even greater satisfaction at follow up. The HIVTSQc (change version)  is assessing the change in patients’ satisfaction 
between their previous and their current treatment within the same group.  
Total score for HIVTSQs ranges from 0 -66. Higher scores indicate a greater satisfaction 
and a lower score indicate dissatisfaction. Individual scores range from 0-6.  HIVTSQc total score ranges from - 33 to 33. A higher score indicate improvement in 
satisfaction with treatment; lower scores indicate a greater deterioration in satisfaction with 
treatment; a score of 0 represents no change. Individual items scores range from - 3 to 3 ( -
3= much less satisfied now, 3= much more satisfied now). 
12.12.6.4.  Perception of Injection (PIN)  
The Perception of Injection (PIN) questionnaire explores the bother of pain at the injection site and ISR, anxiety before and after injection (SC vs IM), willingness to receive an HIV injectable treatment the following visit and satisfaction with the mode of treatment administration of individuals receiving injection and perceptions of individuals associated 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
295 
 with receiving injections. The PIN questionnaire was derived from the Vaccines' 
Perception of Injection (VAPI) questionnaire ( Chevat , 2009), and adapted for HIV -infected 
patients who will receive the CAB LA and RPV LA regimen. This measure contains 21 items that measure pain at injection site, local site reactions, impact on functioning and willingness to pursue injectable treatment outside of a clinical trial. Scores range from 1 to 5, and questions are phrased in such a way as to ensure that 1 always equated with the most favourable perception of vaccination, and 5 the most unfavourable. 
12.12.6.5.  Preference Questionnaire  
A preference question was used to assess patients’ preference, and reasons for preference, for the SC abdominal injections compared with IM gluteal injections. The “Preference” questionnaire will include a single item question evaluating preference of HIV treatment and the attributes supporting this preference. 
12.12.6.6.  Reason for switch questionnaire.  
A single item question will be used to assess reasons participants agreed to switch to a SC injection from their current IM injection at screening.  
12.12.6.7.  Interest in potential self -administration option  
A single item question will be used to assess participants interest in potential upcoming option for self-administering the SC injection. Response options will be evaluated using a likert scale ranging from: “Not at all interested” to “Extremely interested ”. 
12.12.7.  Sub- Study Treatment  
12.12.7.1.  Sub-Study Amendment: Investigational product and Other Study 
Treatment  
Please refer to Section  6.1.3. Cabotegravir Injectable Suspension (CAB LA) and Section 
6.1.4. Rilpivirine Injectable Suspension (RPV LA) included in the main FLAIR protocol. 
12.12.7.2.  Sub-Study Dosage and Administration  
NOTE:  All injection visits during the sub -study should be kept to the same projected visit 
schedule as in the parent study. 
Participants who enter into the SC Abdominal Injection Phase will receive a SC injection 
of CAB LA (2  mL; 400 mg) and RPV LA (2 mL; 600 mg) on Day 1. Subsequent SC 
injections with CAB LA 400 mg (2  mL) and RPV LA 600 mg (2  mL) will occur every 4 
weeks ( -7 days).  Participants who receive SC injections for a total of 12 weeks during the 
SC Abdominal Injection Phase will return to the clinic 4 weeks later ( -7 days) to receive 
their first IM gluteal injections (at Week 12) of CAB LA (2  mL; 400 mg) and RPV LA 
(2 mL; 600 mg) during the Return to Gluteal Injection Phase. The subsequent gluteal 
injection with CAB LA 400 mg (2  mL) and RPV LA 600 mg (2  mL) will occur 4 weeks 
later (±-7 days) at Week 16. Gluteal injections and all assessments administered at the 
Week 20 visit will be considered part of the parent study.  
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
296 
 The interval between injection visits will be limited to a maximum of 4 weeks during the 
SC Abdominal Injection Phase, and 5 weeks during the Return to Gluteal Injection Phase. The Medical Monitor must be contacted to discuss individual participant case ma nagement 
if the length of time between injections exceeds or is projected to exceed these intervals.  
During both the SC Abdominal Injection Phase and the Return to Gluteal Injection Phase, 
CAB injections should be given on the left side of the body and RPV injections should be given on the right side of the body.  
12.12.7.3.  Oral Bridging During the Sub-Study  
Oral bridging will not be allowed during the sub- study as it will interfere with data 
interpretation in the SC injection phase. If oral bridging is needed for any reason, the participant must be withdrawn from the sub- study and either continue onto the par ent 
FLAIR study or transition to commercial drug supply if locally available. 
12.12.8.  Sub- Study Data Management  
Please refer to Section 8. 12.12.9.  Sub- Study Statistical Considerations and Data Analyses  
12.12.9.1.  Statistical Hypotheses  
The primary objective of this sub- study is to evaluate the pharmacokinetics of cabotegravir 
LA (200 mg/mL) and rilpivirine (RPV) LA (300 mg/mL) for monthly dosing as a SC 
injection in the anterior abdominal muscle versus an IM injection into the gluteal muscle in HIV -1 infected participants currently enrolled in the FLAIR study. 
An estimation approach will be taken and point estimates and confidence intervals will be constructed for the ratio of the geometric mean of SC abdominal injection PK parameters to the geometric mean of the IM gluteal injection PK parameters.  
12.12.9.2.  Sample Size Considerations  
The sample size of 30 -50 subjects is deemed sufficient to evaluate the geometric mean ratio 
(SC abdominal injection vs IM gluteal injection) of PK parameters and to assess the safety, tolerability, virologic responses and patient reported outcomes during 12 weeks of the SC abdominal injection phase.  
Although a larger sample size is not needed solely to assess the various PK parameters, 
the larger sample size of 30 -50 will allow a more robust analysis regarding the safety of 
CAB/RPV when administered subcutaneously. Additionally, the larger sample size will provide more insight into subgroup analyses for safety, allowing for a higher likelihood of having more than a few participants in a certain age or BMI category.   
Sample size calculations assume the treatment ratio is 1 with confidence intervals within 
0.8-1.25 and a steady state concentration coefficient of variation of 0.4. Assuming 40 
participants, a CV of 0.4, and power of at least 80%, and a true ratio of 1 we would expect a 90% confidence interval of approximately (0.831, 1.203) on the original scale. 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
297 
 Power  Total N  Alpha  
0.70668  30 0.05 
0.81565  40 0.05 
0.82340  30 0.1 
0.89981  40 0.1 
12.12.9.3.  Sub-Study Analysis Populations  
The Enrolled Population will consist of all participants who sign informed consent into the 
sub-study, excluding screen failures.  
The Safety Population will consist of all enrolled participants who receive at least one SC 
injection. This population will be used to summarize safety, virologic response , and health outcomes endpoints. 
The Pharmacokinetic Concentration (PC) Population will consist of all participants who 
received at least one CAB and/or RPV SC injection and provide at least one non- missing 
CAB and/or RPV plasma concentration value during the sub-study.  
The Pharmacokinetic Parameter (PP) Population will consist of all participants who 
received at least one CAB and/or RPV SC injection and have at least one evaluable PK parameter estimated. PK samples that may be affected by protocol deviations will be reviewed  by the study team to determine whether or not the sample will be excluded.
  
12.12.9.4.  Primary Analysis  
The primary analysis is to compare the abdominal SC injection with  gluteal IM injection using the ratio of the geometric mean of SC injection to the geometric mean of IM injection for a PK parameter within each analyte (CAB, RPV). The primary PK parameter s of 
interest include concentrations at the end of the dosing interval [Ctau], concentrations 1-
week post dose [~Cmax], and area under the curve for the dosing interval [AUC (0- tau)] 
(Table 25).  CAB and RPV concentrations and parameters will be summarized 
descriptively .  No formal bioequivalence testing will be performed.  
 Following log- transformation, C
max, Ctau and AUC(0- tau) will be separately analyzed by 
analyte using a mixed effects model with fixed effect term for type of injection (SC, gluteal) and and BMI (≥30 Kg/m
2, <30 Kg/m2) in addition to a random effect term for subject. As 
it is suspected that varying participant BMI may impact the PK concentration distribution, BMI is being included in the model as a covariate to control for any potential impact beyond the effect of injection type. In each model, only participants with PK parameter 
estimates from corresponding both SC and gluteal injections are included. For example, in the model for comparing C
max between the first  CAB SC injection vs gluteal CAB 
injection, only participants with C max estimates from both first CAB SC injection and CAB 
gluteal injection are included.   
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
298 
 Point estimates and their associated 90% confidence intervals will be constructed for the 
differences between the SC injection and the gluteal injection. The point estimates and their associated 90% confidence intervals from the log -transformed analysis will then be back -
transformed to provide point estimates and 90% confidence intervals for the ratios between the SC injection and the gluteal injection on the original scale. This analysis will be performed using the PK Parameter (PP) population.  
Slope of the Ctau  following the last IM through 3rd SC injection will also be determined 
in an attempt to assess changes in steady state conditions established previously.

12.12.9.5.  Secondary and Exploratory Analyses  
The proportion of participants with HIV -1 RNA ≥50 c/mL and HIV -1 RNA <50 c/mL at 
Week 12 of the SC injection phase will be summarized using FDA Snapshot algorithm for the Safety population in the sub- study. Proportion of participants with protocol -defined 
confirmed virologic failures at Week 12 will also be summarized.  The proportion of participants reporting AEs will be tabulated for each injection type. The following summaries of AEs will be provided: 
• Incidence and severity of ISRs and AEs of special interest during the SC injection phase  
• Proportion of participants who discontinue treatment due to ISRs and proportion of AEs 
of special interest during the SC injection phase • Incidence and severity of AEs not of special interest  
• Incidence of SAEs  
• Change from baseline (latest non- missing value prior to the first SC injection)  
in laboratory parameters will be summarized by visit through the end of the SC phase. • The incidence of observed genotypic and phenotypic resistance to NRTIs and INIs, PIs, 
and NNRTIs will be summarized for subjects meeting confirmed virologic failure criteria.  
 
The health outcomes analyses include analyses of data collected from the following questionnaires, HIVTSQ (both s and c versions), NRS, PIN, and Preference between SC and gluteal injections. The reasons for switch to SC from IM injections will be assessed, 
as well as the interest in a potential option for self -administration of SC injections. Further 
details will be provided in the RAP. Health Outcomes assessments will be s ummarized, 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
299 
 where applicable, by study drug (CAB and RPV), domain, and item.  
 
12.12.9.6.  Sub-Study Interim Analysis 1: ISR Monitoring/Pausing Criteria  
As mentioned in Section 12.12.2.2. an early interim analysis (Interim Analysis 1) will take place to assess the rate of ISRs of interest after 50% of participants (equating to 25 out of the expected 50) have experienced their first SC injection with a follow-up Week 1. An in- stream safety  data cut will be performed for ISR data including site reports of 
details of ISRs of interest. The posterior probability that the rate of ISRs of interest being >0.05 will be calculated based on ISRs of interest collected through Week 1 for each participa nt. A target rate of 0.05 was chosen as it would be the equivalent of >1 
participant out of 25 having an ISR of interest. If the Bayesian posterior probability that the true rate of ISRs of interest is >0.05 is low (< 5%), then individual ISRs will undergo standard safety review. However, if the Bayesian posterior probability that the true rate of ISRs of interest is >0.05 is high ( >5%), then a formal review of all ISR safety data will take place by the VSLC with the potential consideration to pause SC injections. As enrollment will be staggered by country, if 3 participants experience an ISR of interest prior to 25 participants reaching the Week 1 visit, VSLC review will automatically be triggered as 3 out of 25, or a sub-study rate of 0.12, would lead to the posterior probability of the rate of ISRs of interest >0.05 being >5%. Otherwise, VSLC will only be triggered based on the interim posterior probability. An evidence threshold of 5% gives us 95% confidence that the true rate of ISRs of interest is not >0.05 should our interim posterior probability not trigger a decision to bring forth formal VSLC review.  If 1 or 2 participants experience an ISR of interest, these individual cases will be assessed and discussed with the FLAIR Medical Monitor and the Cli nical Development Lead for 
the CAB Treatment Program to determine whether to continue SC dosing for such participants.  
 
12.12.9.7.  Sub-Study Interim Analysis 2: Week 9 Safety and PRO Review  
A second interim analysis (Interim Analysis 2) will focus on safety, tolerability and selected PROs and will not include PK related analyses. The interim analysis will allow for an early assessment of the main safety parameters (ISR type and rate; AEs/SAEs , 
safety related labs including eGFR, ALT, AST, total bilirubin, haematology, and basic chemistry) and PROs (preference and NRS) being assessed in the sub-study.
 
Interim Analysis 2 will take place when 50% of enrolled participants have completed their sub-study Week 9 visit. The analysis will consist of an internal review of key safety/tolerability and preference endpoints in order to assist in compound development. No formal stopping decisions will be made. No formal data cleaning activities will occur. Data will be processed instream with what is available at the time of the data cut. Queries will be issued as needed.  
12.12.10.  Sub- Study Pharmacokinetics  
Pharmacokinetic analysis will be the responsibility of the Clinical Pharmacology  
Modeling & Simulation Department (CPMS), GSK. Individual Plasma CAB and RPV 
TMF-16441767  CONFIDENTIAL  201584  
  Protocol Amendment 09  
300 
 concentration -time data will be analyzed by non- compartmental methods with WinNonlin 
5.2 or higher. Calculations will be based on the actual sampling times recorded during the 
study.  The following pharmacokinetic parameters will be determined for each int erval, as 
data permit: maximum concentration (Cmax), time to Cmax (tmax), area under the plasma concentration -time curve through the end of the dosing interval (AUC( 0-tau), and 
concentration at the end of the dosing interval ( Ct).  
 Plasma concentration data will be summarized descriptively by analyte and injection type and presented in graphical and/or tabular form.  Parameters will be summarized by analyte and injection type, Cmax, AUC ( 0-tau) and Ct treatment comparisons (see Table 25); tmax 
will not be compared statistically.  All pharmacokinetic data (both CAB and RPV) will be stored in the Archives, GSK Pharmaceuticals, R&D.  Additional analyses including modelling, simulation and external validation may be performed to assist in the c linical 
interpretation of these data and will be reported separately.
